Free Talk

Talking About Fasting After Dinner 217

— Xu

I don't know if it's because tonight's food wasn't very appetizing, or because he wasn't in a good mood. After eating two bowls of rice soaked in water, he threw his chopsticks on the table, pushed the bowl to the edge of the table, and said, "I'm not eating anymore!"

Today is January 6, 1933. The sky is gloomy, and moldy water drips from the eaves all day long. Sitting at home is a bit depressing. In addition, it's the first month of the year, and the newspaper workers have also stopped working. We are practically isolated from the world as if locked in a desolate temple. But today, news arrived that Shanhaiguan has fallen, and Tianjin is also in danger. This is truly both laughable and infuriating. The non-resistance general is going to resist to the very end, right? The long-term resistance government is going to sing the tune of long-term resistance for a long time, right? Since Shanhaiguan has been occupied, can Tianjin still be relied upon? Can Beijing still be relied upon? After North China falls, can Nanjing still struggle? Ah, we are becoming slaves to a foreign country! Ah, another national crisis has arrived!

What use is our shouting? What road can we take? Thinking of these difficult problems to solve, I feel a bit like laughing and crying at the same time.

"Another period of national crisis?"

During dinner, none of us spoke. But when he threw his chopsticks on the table and said he wasn't eating anymore, our conversation gradually turned back to the same topic.

"Why?" I asked. "Do you want to fast?"

"Reduce food. Reduce food to save the country!"

"Didn't Wang ×× fast last time? He became famous overnight."

"Ha!"

"It's really interesting. Who cares if you starve to death!"

"Actually, he was still eating. When the students from Beiping came to Nanjing, he was still eating on the train!"

"That's a good method. It's not worth it to really starve to death for this kind of thing! However, it's an appropriate time to show off."

"You could do it too. A special dispatch from Shanghai could immediately report that Professor So-and-so of So-and-so University, grieving the loss of Yuguan and lamenting the daily decline of the nation, has begun a fast from today and urgently urges the authorities to send troops to resist..."

"It's really worth trying!"

"And news reporters will immediately come to interview you."

"Someone will immediately come to write about your daily life. Ha, ha!"

"News reporters can also interview your wife," Old Chen said, laughing.

"At that time, you can hide to avoid trouble and refuse to meet," I said, also laughing. (To be continued)

Japan's Shift from Rule of Law to Rule of Force 218

— Yu Dafu

The Japanese political arena has always been a fighting arena for warlords. Before the Meiji Restoration, among the dictatorial so-called shoguns and regents, which one was not a violent warlord? For 2,500 years, except for a few outstanding talents like Empress Jingu and Prince Shotoku, who used the imperial throne to make some suggestions, has the Japanese imperial family, which they boast as being unbroken for myriad generations, ever had any power in politics? A century ago, the sudden arrival of the black ships and the cannons of the red-haired foreigners shattered the dreams of the dwarves. Thus, the unified situation of "revere the emperor and expel the barbarians" and "returning power to the emperor" finally succeeded.

After the Restoration, the ignorant warlords, compelled by the national trend, pressured by world trends, and inspired by the perseverance of the civilian government faction, did not dare to be leaders of the military and destroy this constitutional government, which had been built with much bloodshed, sacrifice, and difficult management. For seventy years, the reason why this small island nation was able to dominate East Asia and act ferociously in the world was all thanks to the spirit of the rule of law.

Now, parliamentary politics is also exhausted, the anxiety arising from the vast gap between rich and poor has expanded, and coupled with the stimulation of new world trends and the incompetence of key figures in the political center, the warlords, who have been hiding their ambitions for a long time, will naturally take this opportunity to rise up and seize power. The rampant assassinations, the activities of the Kokuhonsha, the exposure of the Communist Party, and the dispatch of troops to Southern Manchuria—aren't these all evidence of the warlords seizing power? Japan is at a crossroads, on the eve of shifting from the rule of law to the rule of force. Not only is this clear to us onlookers, but even the old Japanese statesman Yukio Ozaki has stated in London that the warlords will soon practice dictatorship and that Japan's national fortune will soon come to an end. Although I am not a prophet, I believe that Japan will undergo tremendous changes within five years. First, the rampant warlords and the complete destruction of the legal order, followed by the uprising of the oppressed masses and the transformation of the Japanese state and political system. Let us wait and see! The bloody red light will surely shine from this land of the rising sun to the whole world!

Their Sorrows 219

— Su

There is a wonderful Chinese saying, I don't know who came up with it, called "a talented scholar matches a beautiful woman." Translated into modern language, it means "a cosmopolitan man matches a modern girl," or, loosely translated, "a handsome guy pairs with a pretty girl," which is almost the same.

We can cite many examples of this "talented scholar matching a beautiful woman" pattern. In the West, there's Dante and Beatrice, Keats and Fanny Brawne, Rossetti and Siddal, Shelley and Mary, Galsworthy and Ada. In the East, there's Bai Juyi and Fan Su and Xiao Man, Jiang Baishi and Xiao Hong, Wang Xianzhi and Peach Leaf, Han Yi and Zhangtai Liu...

It's really as Milton said, "Men are the embodiment of strength, while women are made of gentleness and charm." In historical romances, it can almost be said that men sell their talent, while women sell their beauty. Men can be a bit ugly, but women must have an oval face. If a man is both handsome and charming, that's the icing on the cake, but if a woman has talent, it becomes superfluous. Don't those cunning and hypocritical moralists sing the high-pitched tune of "lack of talent in a woman is a virtue"?

In the past, talented women almost always lived in sorrow. This is not fate, but the result of oppression and contempt in society. The beautiful Lady Reigate had star-like men surrounding her. The famous professor Sofia Kovalevskaya lamented, "Why does no one love me? I am superior to most women, but the most ordinary women are loved, while I am not!" We can hear the sighs of these unfortunate, talented women everywhere.

Opening the history of Chinese literature, famous female writers all spent their lives in sorrow. Their works are the crystallization of their sorrows. Our familiar female poet Zhu Shuzhen even titled her poetry collection "Gut-wrenching Collection" and expressed the indignant words, "A woman writing literature is truly a crime, how much more so to sing of the moon and chant of the wind!" This is the typical unfortunate "talented woman" of the East.

The great female lyricist Li Qingzhao's whole life was a sad poem. When we read her famous work "Slow, Slow Tune," the indescribable, unresolvable sorrow, the boundless sadness hidden in her heart, are all left on paper by her genius.

The female poet He Shuangqing, also called "sorrow as the fountain of her life", of the early Qing Dynasty, wrote on a reed leaf to her uncle; "Remembering the night without joy, facing spring with difficulty smiling, the peach blossoms quickly large, the bamboo greens constantly disappointed, how could it not be wished that people would sing of tears!" This kind of scene is truly "can not but resent".

In the West, the English female poet Elizabeth Barrett Browning, when she was still a young girl, wrote her own psychology in her novel, saying through the mouth of the female poet in the book, "Ah! Heaven! When a woman sits alone at home on a winter night and hears the praise of the whole country from afar, only you can know this sorrow. There is no kiss on our lips, our eyes are always wet, because no one cares why we weep." If the great poet Robert Browning had not accepted her love, then she would probably not only have written the famous poem "The Cry of the Children," but perhaps also a "The Cry of the Maidens"!

The German female poet Adele Schopenhauer, the sister of the philosopher Schopenhauer, once wrote very proudly in her diary about her own sadness: "Who is more lovable than me? In love, who can find greater happiness than me? But this is over, forever over! I can only stay in my lonely tomb." This sad life fostered her "arrogance and loneliness."

In addition, the Russian female writer Alexandra Kollontai, in her great work "Red Love," wrote about the sorrow of revolutionary women in love. The heroine in the book is probably Kollontai in her youth. The French writer Madame de Staël also lamented that her fame brought her an unfortunate fate.

Of course, outside this circle of "talented scholar matching a beautiful woman," we can still find pairs like "Qin Guan and Su Xiaomei." And in this new era, we can find even more. Isn't the American female poet Edna St. Vincent Millay living her life of love? This Miss So-and-so is a good example.

The times are constantly changing. We firmly believe that the era of "handsome guys and pretty girls" must pass, and the era of "great men and healthy women" must surely come. The introduction of this new era will surely bring about the day when their sorrows are eliminated.

The World's Largest Airplane 220

— Hong Xingchi

The German aircraft Dornier Do X, number thirty-eight, is the world's largest aircraft to date. It has now been completed and has begun flying between Berlin and London.

This aircraft is designed solely for carrying passengers. It has two large cabins in the middle and a smoking room at the tail, as smoking near the engines could be dangerous. There is also a small cabin that can seat two people under the wings, specially designed for passengers who like to see the scenery. The fare is, of course, higher. In total, it can carry thirty-four passengers, plus a helmsman, a co-helmsman, an engineer, two pilots, a radio operator, and a supervisor, for a total of forty-one people.

The entire aircraft has four engines, each with 650 horsepower. Two engines are hidden in each wing. The four fuel tanks are also two on each side. The engine room is like a large ship, with very thorough protection. When flying over the sea, this aircraft has a speed of 115 miles per hour, and 58 miles per hour over land. The aircraft is also equipped with two pairs of large wheels underneath, so it can also drive on the ground. Because the aircraft is too large, it cannot be pushed. When fully loaded with passengers, it weighs a total of 31 tons. The wings are shorter than the fuselage, so when flying in the air, it looks like a short-winged eagle.

Editor's Office 221

Lie Wen recently suffered a misfortune: his beloved wife Bingzhi (Ye Ying), from classmate to spouse, traveled to Europe for five years, sharing hardships together, hoping to graduate and return to establish a family and serve society. Unexpectedly, she died recently from puerperal fever due to malpractice by an American quack in a hospital in western Shanghai. For the past two weeks, this column has been edited by Mr. Yang Xingzhi, allowing it to continue to meet with readers, which is deeply appreciated. Now that my wife's funeral is roughly over, Lie Wen will return to the office to work as usual from today. However, my heart is filled with grief, and it is difficult to express my struggles. I sincerely hope that talented people at home and abroad will contribute excellent works so that the content of this publication will become richer day by day. This would not only be the good fortune of this publication but also the good fortune of the future of Chinese culture. Respectfully, Li Lie Wen

Long Novel

The Crossroads of Era and Love (Continued) 222

— Zhang Ziping

"That's the church's outdoor missionary team."

They walked towards the crowd.

"…Saints like brave soldiers, marching forward in battle! The cross is our banner!…"

He clearly understood the meaning of the song they were singing. Because the previous Friday, Cao Shiguang had taken him to the church and he had heard them sing this hymn.

"Ah! Isn't that Pastor Hubbard?"

He saw Pastor Hubbard waving his right hand, conducting his subordinates in singing, while his left hand held a white handkerchief to wipe the sweat from his forehead. His upper and lower lips opened and closed, and his singing was particularly powerful, as loud and high as a bull's bellow.

Mrs. Hezi seemed a little shorter. At that moment, she stood on tiptoe, placed her hands on his shoulders, rested her chin on his shoulder, and looked at the preachers. Her right cheek was almost touching his left cheek. He also felt her breath, which smelled similar to Acetylene Gas. At this moment, he felt a great pressure both physically and mentally. He also felt his blood boiling.

He looked more carefully and saw that under Pastor Hubbard's direction, Cao Shiguang and Liao Haifeng were also stretching their necks and singing hymns. Judging by their spirits, they were very tired, but they had to try their best to sing along. He also saw Cao Shiguang yawning.

"Ah, they are really enthusiastic about preaching."

She said to him with a smile. He smelled a smell similar to Acetylene Gas again. He felt that this breath had an exciting, stimulating effect.

"Ha, ha. That person is yawning!"

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Another Shot of Morphine 223

— Yu

Our Chinese nation seems to be a dying patient, while Japan is like a doctor treating the patient. When a patient is very ill, they are always mentally weak, reluctant to speak, even with eyes closed as if dead, and without smell or sound. The doctor always gives them a shot of morphine at this moment, so that their barely surviving nerves can be energized and have the possibility of excitement. Now, Japan is doing the same to the Chinese nation.

The "September 18th Incident" in Shenyang the year before last was like a sudden shot of morphine! The "January 28th Incident" in Shanghai last year was another shot! The recent "Yuguan Incident" on January 3rd, year 22, was another shot! Originally, the national character of our Republic of China can be said to have been on the verge of decline for a long time! To use a morbid analogy, it had simply reached the point where its breath was barely there and there was no cure. Suddenly, it was given a shot of morphine, which awakened its comatose mind and suddenly realized that a great disaster was imminent and that it was in imminent danger! Only then did it think about struggling and shout out a desolate and painful cry of "Resist Japan and Save the Country." Just as it was riding a wave of excitement and shouting vigorously, another shot came in quick succession! As a result, this continuous drug force filled the whole body from the limbs and bones, and all the nerves became more excited and could not be restrained! Therefore, it simply straightened its throat and shouted loudly! However, as time went by, the effect of the drug gradually faded, the shouting gradually decreased, and eventually its strength weakened and its voice became faint, and it would still return to a state of silence. This neighbor, Japan, saw that our nation was still weak and about to return to its previous state of collapse, so it wanted to be kind and gave it another shot! Presumably, our nation will now rely on this rapid and fierce drug force and will get another moment of excitement, shouting very hard, and the lively situation will certainly not be less than before, and its duration, at least to say, should be extended by five minutes!

However, the nature of morphine will eventually fade away; moreover, it is a poisonous substance, and if too many shots are given, there is a danger of harming life! Therefore, relying on morphine to be excited is not the same thing after all!

And finally, I still want to ask a question: Is our Chinese nation really a nation that only knows how to be excited after taking morphine? Is our government really paralyzed to the extreme and still does not know how to be excited after taking morphine?

Literature and Art

Ode to Snow 224

— Tinggui

Sighing about the rise and fall of events, the jade tower is again full of mountains. A green sword can cut stone, but it is difficult to split the barrier of beauty. The mountains are full of white snow containing the breath of spring, and the cold plums beside the pavilion welcome the crowd to bloom.

Ignorant stubborn stones undergo dramatic changes, nodding and idly imagining an old monk coming.

Relief 225

— Chen Zhou

What is going on? The Third Detachment telegraphed the day before yesterday, saying that yesterday they could go to the Volunteer Army Support Association to collect bullets, and after receiving them, they would send them immediately. Why haven't they been sent yet today? Could it be that they encountered enemy troops on the road and had an accident? Or did they not receive them?

We are all anxious. Originally, we didn't have many bullets. In order to capture this Luotian Fort, we fought with the enemy for three days and three nights, and we really spent a lot. If the Third Detachment doesn't send the bullets again, won't we lose all our previous efforts?

Fortunately, the enemy didn't rush over, only fired a few sentinel guns. We were lying in the cold trenches, motionless. Sometimes they fired a few shots, but this was just a bluff. In fact, it is best for us not to fire. At this time, our bullets are so precious! The enemy's iron birds come to our positions from time to time to scout and throw grenades. We ignored them. We were afraid that they would know that we had no bullets!

We are looking forward to and longing for the arrival of the Third Detachment's relief as soon as possible.

However, in the afternoon, our hope turned into despair!

"Brothers! You have probably all heard that the Third Detachment just telegraphed to say that the Volunteer Army Support Association doesn't have many bullets left and refuses to issue them. If they refuse to issue them, what will we do?" Captain Wu said to us, "Do we want to die? Or do we want to live?"

"We want to live!"

"We want to live!"

"We want to live! There are only two paths: one is to retreat, and the other is!" Captain Wu said,

"Retreat? I will never retreat! We spent three days and three nights to capture this Luotian Fort. How can we lightly give it up?" Lao Cheng said anxiously,

"Yes, we will never give up Luotian Fort! Otherwise, won't all our previous efforts be wasted?"

"There is another path!" Captain Wu continued, "What is it?" It was Lao Cheng's voice again,

"Don't shout, listen. That path is! It is to surrender, surrender to the enemy!"

"What? Surrender?" It was Lao Cheng again,

"If we surrender, everyone will be high-ranking officials! We will all have status!"

"Well! If we surrender to the enemy, without even asking whether we will be officials, aren't we becoming soldiers for the enemy and fighting against our own Third Detachment?" It was Deputy Captain Wu's voice,

"Bang!" With a sound, Captain Wu fell!

"Brothers! When should we kill this kind of traitor if not now! He has been killed by me now! I say, let's use our last few rows of bullets and charge forward! Seize their bullets, okay?" Deputy Captain Wu said loudly,

"Okay! Charge out!" We all fixed bayonets on our rifles,

The Wandering Singer 226

— Xiyin

Two people, one in front and one behind, playing fluent erhus, walked slowly from the east end of the street to the west end. Several children followed behind, enjoying his beautiful voice. The entire street did not have a single person willing to pay them to sing. The two of them, one was an elderly man with white hair and beard, and the other was a thin and tall teenager. Both of them had faces full of wind and frost, and their clothes were ragged and their appearances were extremely haggard. It could be seen that they were people who were busy on the road all year round to live their lonely and tasteless lives. Alas! How noble is art? Driven by life, there is no appropriate time or place to express it, but it wanders in the alleys and streets, seeking a meal. Don't say there are no like-minded people, but they also have to endure people's ridicule, ridiculing him as a fallen person. Alas! The end of art has been determined!

The old man looked around and walked into a small teahouse with the young man, sitting next to a table by the wall. The old man first tuned the erhu, and then began to play and sing: "I am a crazy person, and there is more sorrow after entering the world! I can't stand the chaos of society, and all I see is you pushing me!…" He sang very sadly, and although no one in the room understood his meaning, they listened because the tone of their singing was very pleasant to the ear.

"…What are you doing for? Nothing more than money and status! Confused thoughts and mental fatigue are all caused by these two things! How many ambitious people have been squeezed out and cannot be successful!…" My heart was shaken by his singing, and I also felt the chaos of society, as if there were endless words to say. Suddenly, with a "bang," the string broke. The two of them didn't ask for money, stood up, and walked away with the broken-stringed qin. On the road, they simply sang wildly and unrestrainedly. Few passers-by paid attention to him, thinking that they were engaged in the lowly profession of singing and were not worth paying attention to; and they laughed at them as truly crazy people. Only a few innocent and uninhibited children still followed, almost without touching the ground.

The Son of a Treacherous Merchant 227

— Zhuxi

The sound of pouring chamber pots in the city broke the silence of the winter morning.

It came from a mansion standing beside the main road.

"Madam, something bad happened!…Young master is gone!" The maid's shout interrupted the snoring in the whole house.

What? Don't…talk nonsense!…Where did he go?…"Mrs. Wang woke up from a sweet dream, and hurriedly sat up, trembling with fright and cold, and asked Zhang Ma, the reporter, who was standing by her bed, anxiously: "How do you know?"

"Madam, just now I went to his room to clean up, and saw that the things were thrown in a mess. As for the person, I searched for a long time but couldn't find him!" Zhang Ma answered quickly.

"Go and call the master up, quick!" Mrs. Wang ordered, hurriedly put on a large fur cheongsam, got out of bed, put on her slippers, and ran to Damin's bedroom on the third floor, secretly guessing in her heart: "Could this beast have left just because his father scolded him a few words last night?…Oh! Damin, have you left me?…It's all those harmful schools that have turned a good child like this after reading books for two years. What anti-Japanese association, student union, everything is learned from others like dogs.…I knew earlier that nothing good would come of it,…Alas! Who would listen to a mother's words there? Last night, he even had a fight with his father,…" Mrs. Wang stepped into Damin's room and saw the suitcases and clothes thrown on the ground,…She was sure that her son had left, and began to cry loudly.

"What? Did the beast leave?…Good! I'm unlucky, I raised him," Mr. Wang strode into the room, saying angrily. Behind him stood his beloved concubine and Zhang Ma.

"Is there a letter?…Hmm! Here." Mr. Wang picked up the letter on the table at random, opened it, and read it softly:

Parents: I have nothing to say. Last night, I asked you not to recognize the enemy as your father and sell enemy goods, but I was scolded by you for being talkative, saying that if you don't do this business, how will you eat. Father! I can't believe that people who don't act as Japanese dogs can't survive! Isn't this greed for profit? [The disease of the Chinese people]…Father, mother, good land has been easily given away by scoundrels. Are you still doing business? Are you still living?…Alas! Father! A happy family is built on a complete country! I cannot sit idly by while the lovable volunteer soldiers who are sacrificing themselves to kill the enemy are gradually being killed by the enemy; I do not recognize that the citizens of the great Republic of China will become slaves of a fallen country. I only know that only "resistance" can save China, so I am leaving! I have left my "small self" without hesitation to save my "big self"! Father! Isn't that right? If one more useless me dies, one less respectable volunteer soldier will die! That is also prolonging your fate for a moment!…Haha! Dying on the battlefield is much more glorious than dying on the Bund! The clothes, jewelry, and cash of about 5,000 yuan that I took away are considered my father's "generous donation" to the volunteer soldiers as military expenses! Goodbye! Respectfully,

Wake up quickly! Your son, Damin, farewell.

After reading the letter, Mr. Wang sighed deeply, saw the newspaper on the table, which was full of large-sized lead letters: Yuguan was lost, the League of Nations planned a compromise, the Japanese army attacked Kaifeng Lu, and attacked Chaoyang Nanling. The volunteer army fought hard waiting for reinforcements…

He seemed to be somewhat moved, remorseful, and grief-stricken, occupying his heart. Tears welled up from his eyelashes, he threw the letter, and lay down on the sofa.

"Where did he go?" Mrs. Wang asked, crying.

"Brave Damin! My good son, a good citizen of the country,…He…he joined the volunteer army…to kill Japanese devils!…I…was wrong…I was wrong!" Mr. Wang couldn't help crying out loud.

From then on, the Volunteer Army Support Association added two backbone members [Mr. and Mrs. Wang].

Slave 228

— Dongxin

"You are simply slaves!" A Chinese teacher often said this to a class of students who made a lot of noise during Chinese class. Indeed, they were too much during Chinese class. The blackboard was covered with many sentences and pictures insulting the teachers, and they made all kinds of strange noises. It was simply not like a class. No wonder the Chinese teacher couldn't help but be angry.

The Chinese teacher was a teacher with profound knowledge of Chinese classics and was loyal and dedicated. He didn't have the bad habits of other teachers, such as asking for leave, arriving late, and leaving early. He spoke loudly and clearly. He had these qualities, so he became one of the best teachers in our school.

"…" The class bell was ringing, and his footsteps had already entered the classroom. After taking attendance, he began to raise his voice, trying to arouse the students' interest in Chinese class. However, the students' carelessness towards Chinese class seemed to be hereditary. No matter which expert who deeply studies education, I am afraid that they can no longer break this bad habit. So the students habitually talked, dozed off, and read novels…

Time passed minute by minute, and the sound of students talking also became louder and louder. The teacher really couldn't bear it anymore, so he put down his books and tried to persuade them with sweet words. But the result was not only like playing the lute to a cow, but also won a booing protest.

"If any of you don't want to attend class, please leave…Don't you think about your parents using their hard-earned money to send you to school, hoping that you will achieve something in the future…If you don't want to study, then please ask your parents to donate your tuition to the Northeast Volunteer Army to kill the enemy, so as to avoid…Good baby, give me North China!"

"That teacher spoke more and more angrily. His face was as red as fire, because the students didn't listen to his teachings, and the sounds of ridicule and conversation merged together, and the classroom was like a market.

"You only make trouble in Chinese class. Why aren't you as disciplined as you are in English class?…You are afraid of foreigners and look down on Chinese people. You are not worthy of talking about patriotism, and you are even less worthy of being the masters of China in the future…You are slaves of foreigners…" The students did not sympathize with this teacher at all. I often heard that he was pessimistic about the country's future because of the students' mischief, and even often shed tears of pain.

Class was over, and the teacher had not finished speaking, but the students had already rushed out like a tide.

Next was English class. The classroom was very quiet, and there was not even a sound of coughing. They treated this green-eyed, high-nosed foreigner as if he were sacred and inviolable, respecting him even more than their parents, let alone talking, they didn't even dare to move. Then it was the same dismissal, but the situation was different. The students seemed not to have heard the class.

"Next time prepare twenty pages. Do you all understand?" The foreign teacher stood up and said this. "Yes, sir," the students answered in unison, and then one by one, like an army marching in formation, followed the foreign teacher out of the classroom. I couldn't help but recall the Chinese teacher's words "slave." One hour's work had already been realized before our eyes.

Sacrificing for the Country 229

— Hongwei

Although he was old, his heart was still as hot as when he was young. Especially for national affairs, he paid more attention than anything else. He was often indignant and could not control himself when he saw foreign aggression against his country.

One day, he learned that his country had diplomatically broken off relations and officially declared war on a certain country. So he was overjoyed and said to his four sons: "Our country has been subjected to all kinds of aggression by a certain country, and it has been unbearable. Now they have again taken the opportunity to shoot and kill many of our compatriots, violating international conventions and arousing the public anger of the world. And their diplomatic authorities, relying on the military strength of their country's navy and army as backing, do not speak of justice at all. As a result, negotiations broke down and led to war. This war is related to the survival of our country. I am old and can no longer go to the battlefield to serve the country. You are all young and strong, and it is good to contribute to the country and win back sovereignty; I wonder who is willing to join the army?"…He had not finished speaking, and the four sons had already enthusiastically shouted: "I am willing to go! I am willing to go!" He couldn't help but stroke his beard and smile: "Good brave young men!"

After he sent his sons away, he did not stop inquiring about the news of the war for a single day. A week later, it happened that a friend came from the battlefield and told him: "We won the battle! But one of your sons died." He smiled when he heard this and said: "This is a very good thing!" A few days later, someone else said to him: "We won another battle! But another one of your sons also died." He still happily said: "A very good thing!" Later, his remaining two sons also continued to die in battle. In this way, all four of his sons died. At the same time, a certain country had ceased fighting and asked for peace, voluntarily canceling the unequal treaties previously signed and returning the land previously occupied. He heard that none of his four sons survived, and of course he couldn't help but shed a few tears; but knowing that the result of the war was a victory thanks to the efforts of the country's strong men, he couldn't help but dance and clap his hands. On the day when the army was parading in formation, the old man also waved the bright and splendid, respectable and lovely flag of the Republic of China, which fluttered in the wind, barely lifted his dry and parched throat, and echoed in the midst of the ten-mile-long cheers of thousands of people singing the triumphant song of raising our national prestige, wiping out our national shame, overthrowing imperialism, canceling unequal treaties, and fighting for freedom, equality, and independence.

Shop Clerk Communication

A Shop Clerk's Grievance 230

Editor: Opening the newspaper, we often see words such as "snobbish clerks" and "arrogant clerks" that catch our eyes; we have never seen articles of the "unreasonable customers" type. The editor is inevitably suspected of "partiality." Perhaps this is confused by the so-called "the customer is always right" saying?

I am a salesperson in a nationally famous Shanghai department store and have been working there for almost three years. I have heard, seen, and personally experienced disputes between clerks and customers. Let's analyze the causes of the disputes. Salespeople certainly have shortcomings in their service, but customers also have the bad habit of having a "bad temper." Almost five or six out of ten of the customers who wear Western suits and leather shoes, the so-called intellectuals, seem to have problems with their vocal cords when they patronize: they whistle "shh shh" in their mouths, and at the same time point to the required goods with one index finger, unwilling to "open their mouths." If we sincerely take the goods they need and ask them how much they want to buy, they always use the number of fingers to indicate the number they need.

I really don't understand, do these friends in Western suits think that they are supreme figures, unwilling to talk to people who do business? Or is it because the salesperson did not take the initiative to serve them, so they whistle "shh shh"? Here we want to declare that we are a store where people are free to browse, and we can never be like the clerks in old-fashioned stores, following the customers.

Our store's business is very developed, and customers are often crowded. Therefore, each salesperson has to serve many customers, and naturally there are times when they cannot handle everything. In terms of service, driven by the facts, we inevitably neglect one thing while attending to another; therefore, it causes misunderstandings among customers who cannot understand others, and they say embarrassing words. "You are too snobbish. Don't think that I don't buy many goods. You treat people slowly. You must know that buying a lot or buying a little, we are all your customers…" Really, the words are strict and the reasons are correct. If people with this snobbish point of view heard it, they should sincerely accept their kind advice, but how can we have this bad idea! Our store rules, "merit and demerit awards and punishments" are not based on the amount of business, and there are no bad habits like "commission" in other stores.

Originally, in this situation, we wanted to explain our unavoidable difficulties and ask customers to forgive us; but with busy business, there is really no possibility to explain to them. Editor, please allow me to use your valuable space to explain! Respectfully, Wang Yanqiu.

Editor's note: The kind of customer described in Mr. Wang's letter certainly has the problem of having a "bad temper"; and according to what we know, customers' rudeness is endless. Mr. Wang has tasted this flavor for a long time, and it is only natural that he expresses his grievances.

We must know that shops seek profit from capital, and clerks sell labor. Thinking from the perspective of division of labor and cooperation, they and any class that is considered noble in the present era are all indispensable members of society. If we can thoroughly understand this meaning, then customers will certainly not have arrogant behavior.

Finally, we must also advise Mr. Wang that if you encounter this kind of customer in the future, it is best to explain if you have the opportunity. Otherwise, you don't have to worry about it, because this is their own personality, and it is not worth having the same understanding as them.

Fiction

A Family of Scholars (Continuation 4) 231

— Wang Zhongxian

Madame Xia having previously refused Zhongnan's request to accommodate an outside woman and her child, why would she now graciously permit him to marry a prostitute as a concubine? It turns out that when Zhongnan first wanted to take a concubine, he used edicts such as "Of the three unfilial acts, the greatest is to have no descendants" to persuade her. She then said, "As long as we both try, I am not barren. If I plant the seed, it will eventually bear fruit. If I am still unproductive after the age of forty, then I will have to let you act freely!"

That Miss Xia Airuo Hua was officially married to Master Xia Zhongnan after Madame Xia held her grand fortieth birthday celebration. Whether the name "Ruo Hua" was actually her elegant name used when advertising herself for hire is impossible to verify now, being so far away in the south. We only know that when she married into the Xia family, she brought a superfluous "oil bottle" daughter with her.

Ruo Hua was not very old—only twenty-seven at the time—but she had already experienced much suffering and had taken a great tumble in the world of love. According to what she told Zhongnan:

"I was originally from a good family. My father was a horse trader in the Zhangjiakou area. Because he encountered bandits on the road, a group of horses were all robbed. He lost his capital and went home, becoming ill with paralysis from anger. Soon after, he and my mother died one after the other. I was reduced to prostitution at the age of ten. At fifteen, I started singing and receiving guests in Jiangnan. At that time, I already understood human affairs and knew that being a prostitute was a lowly thing. I wholeheartedly wanted to find a good man to marry. It wasn't until I was seventeen that I found a young man I liked. I saw that he had a handsome appearance and had no wife, but his family was poor. In my heart, I only wanted to live a hard life as husband and wife, but it would be enough if I could gain spiritual comfort. I resolved to marry him and use my savings to support him in his studies. After a few years, I scraped together some money from other customers and asked him to redeem me. I then married him. After living together for a year, I gave birth to a daughter, and that person's bad habits gradually surfaced. It turned out that he had already married a wife in his hometown. He took my money and secretly gambled outside. He often demanded money from me. If I didn't give it to him, he would scold me and hit me. Later, when he saw that my money was used up, he abandoned me. I had no choice but to fall back into prostitution, traveling thousands of miles to this place to make a living. It's all for this daughter that I suffer! If it weren't for her, I wouldn't want to be in this world anymore! I was fooled by a young man the first time I married. I dare not try again lightly, so I would rather marry you, an old man, as a concubine. But my daughter! I have suffered all kinds of hardships for her! I will always keep her by my side. After I marry into your family, I would rather you mistreat me than mistreat her."

Movie Special Edition

An Overview of "Insulting China" Films 232

— Bao Han

Expectations for "The Good Earth"

American films involving Chinese people, such as "The Bitter Tea of General Yen" and "Shanghai Express," have already been sentenced to death. There are countless others that I do not need to go over in detail. However, as far as I know, "The Bitter Tea of General Yen" does not contain any humiliation of China in its story. However, in terms of clothing, makeup, and the portrayal of Chinese people's actions, there are always questionable aspects. If it were shown in Shanghai, it would inevitably be criticized by fastidious film critics.

The content of "Son Daughter" has not been studied, so I dare not comment. However, Ramon Novarro is someone in Hollywood who respects the Chinese. He likes to associate with the Chinese. He says that the Chinese are honest, and it is a blessing to associate with them. Therefore, I don't think Ramon will satirize us in this film. Moreover, Ramon even shaved his head and wore a square-topped watermelon hat to star in this film. It seems that we should not be too demanding in terms of humor. Even if Louis Stone wears a queue, didn't everyone wear a queue with a silk ribbon and call themselves a handsome young man twenty years ago? I think Louis Stone played it very well, but I will reserve a judgment until I see the film.

"The Mask of Fu Manchu" can be said to be of the highest degree of degradation in both content and appearance. The story is absurd, and the acting is even more outrageous. I can assert that this film is specifically for Americans who lack knowledge of the world. It is inexplicable why MGM would do this, but it allows us to further recognize the limitations of their knowledge. (I will briefly introduce the story later.) But we cannot blame them too much because the American people are entirely pleasure-seeking. Although they like to travel, they only do so for sightseeing and entertainment, and they do not genuinely bother to investigate customs and practices. All they know about the Chinese are the Chinatowns in New York and San Francisco. They have never come into contact with high-minded Chinese people. The few Chinese they know are only low-level people in laundries or chop suey restaurants. These people generally do not know propriety and do not care about the dignity of the country.

Now there is a person who has been in China for many years who wrote a novel about the lives of Chinese farmers. This book is the best American work of 1932 (?), and won the Pulitzer Prize that year. Her book has been adapted into a stage play that was popular in New York. This writer is Mrs. Pearl Buck. Her husband, J. Lossing Buck, is the head professor of rural economics and social sciences at Jinling University in Nanjing. Mrs. Buck grew up in China and knows a lot. The name of her book is "The Good Earth." While being busy all day, the author has not yet finished reading it, but I feel that the first few pages depict life in northern villages realistically and profoundly (she depicted the fat butler of a large northern family, with a mole on his face and two or three long hairs that he did not shave off, which shows the author's attention to detail). After the stage play was successful, MGM is going to adapt it into a movie (Mrs. Buck called it Electric Shadows). I hear that it is already in preparation. I cannot help but express a deep expectation. As for what happens next, let's wait and see.

Movie Review and Commentary

Puss in Boots｜Carlton 233

— Ming

This Puss in Boots is the new film at Carlton. The child stars are not the ones we often see. Their performances are very consistent. This film is not ordinary. It is unique in the world of sound films. Perhaps it can be said to be comparable to the silent film "Peter Pan." It is indeed not easy for children to achieve such results in a film.

The plot can be said to be like a long fairy tale novel, and it is not flat. Everywhere, it vividly reveals the "liveliness" of the children. This kind of film changes everyone's taste, and this kind of taste has never been tasted before.

I am not saying how good this film is—it is amazing!—but I feel that even what Jackie Coogan gave us ten years ago, or what Jackie Cooper gives us now, cannot be compared to this film. The reason is that the so-called child prodigy actors in the past played the main role in a film, and adults had to be used as supporting roles. But this time, "Puss in Boots" was filmed by the joint efforts of many children. Of course, the director of this film can also be said to have put in a lot of effort.

There is nothing to criticize in terms of photography, lighting, or set design, but the music is truly wonderful. It can make cold fragments compact and lively.

The child stars not only perform extremely well, but the spirit of the dialogue, to put it bluntly, is simply "little adults." The songs they sing and the dances they dance are also interesting to watch. I deeply believe that this film is most welcome to children. Unfortunately, Carlton's film only has two day showings (the night showing is an Italian stage play). Adults who like children or parents who want their children to be lively can find considerable comfort in this film.

A scene from the new Wufats film "The Fairy in Rainbow Dress," which will be screened at the New Light Grand Theatre tomorrow night.

Talking About "Humane" Thieves 234

— Jing Guan

On a cold and rainy winter night, Star Film Company's new film "Humane Thief" was quietly screened at the Central Theatre. Although it was a non-public screening, I got the news and quickly ran to enjoy the "sneak preview."

After the screening, as I walked out of the Central Theatre, I replayed the film I had seen in my mind and felt that the impression was really good. Now I will write some of my opinions here:

(1) Talking about the director: The director of the film is Wang Xianzai. With his talent, there are many clever and subtle expressions in "Humane Thief." In particular, several interpolations can be said to be exceptionally meaningful and flavorful. For example, the contrast between Zhuang Dade and his son reading books in the film, and the encounter between father and son by the ladder, are all subtle and delightful. Several scenes of Zhuang Zhiqin flirting are imitated very freshly. Strictly speaking, the directing technique of this film is somewhat lacking in "depth," but it is still lively and vivid.

(2) Talking about expressions: Zheng Xiaoqiu's identity is suitable, so he does a very good job. Secondly, Xu Xinyuan, this gentleman, his face is indeed somewhat "serious," but a kind of cunning atmosphere is faintly visible. Speaking of female roles, then Zhu Qiuhen is more competent than Yan Yuexian.

(3) On the idea: This film is very powerful in exposing the dark side of society in terms of consciousness. It bravely pierces through and tears apart the paper mask of "benevolence and morality" of a pseudo-moralist, and clearly points out to us who is the "thief" of "humanity"? Who is the scum of society? Such exposure is naturally needed now.

In a word: This is a domestic film worth watching, so I would like to introduce it to you.

Beautiful Women and Famous Horses | New Light 235

— Ai

Paramount's Wild Horse Mesa is showing on the New Light screen. This film is similar to Chinese martial arts films, but the plot is still worth watching. Although it does not jump out of the scope of American Western life films, it is clearly different from other cowboy life films.

The moral concept in its plot is very rich. First, it shows that the retribution of good and evil is never wrong. Second, it can show that Heaven has the virtue of cherishing life, and it is inhumane to kill even an innocent animal (horse). Third, it is said that the love between men and women and the righteousness of brothers are the right way of human relations.

The performances are very compact. The people in the play can all be realized, especially Randolph Scott, famous for playing martial arts heroes. His horse "Bench" is also very good. Tony (Tom Mix's horse) was injured and cannot work for the screen. Perhaps "Bench" is very promising for the position of "horse star" in the future.

The photography is ordinary. The lighting is mostly outdoor scenes, so there is no artistic merit to speak of. The director is okay, and the dialogue is also very expressive. The interpolation is very appropriate. Only the scenery seems a bit fake, but there are also many real scenes. Large groups of wild horses and vast wilderness are rare in other films.

At first glance, the four characters "Beautiful Women and Famous Horses" will definitely be thought of as a romance film. In fact, love accounts for very little of the film. The "hero worship" doctrine is invisibly latent here.

Audience Chat

Morality? Or System? 237

— Hui Zun

Luckily, after I bought a ticket, the sign "Downstairs is Full" was hung up.

Stepping into the door of the main hall, the noisy sound made me feel a little impatient. Looking at the room again, a courtyard full of people was sitting in the dark. I frowned, searching for an empty seat as if I were about to discover a new continent.

Fortunately, I suddenly found an empty seat in the crowd. I immediately thanked the person sitting next to me and squeezed in sideways.

Just as I was happily preparing to sit down, a young and modern lady sitting next to me suddenly stopped me and said, "Oh! There's someone here."

I sullenly squeezed out again.

The second time I found an empty seat, I was also refused. The third time... the fourth time I encountered the same answer. I also got a little angry and prepared to return the ticket and not watch it.

When I turned around, I unintentionally saw that there was still an empty seat next to the lady. My curiosity was aroused, so I stood next to her and waited...

Five minutes passed, and the movie was about to begin. The lady also refused several people, and the seat was indeed still empty. So I boldly walked in again.

Just as the lady was about to speak, I stopped her and said:

"I'm very sorry. When the person for this seat comes, I'll let him have it."

The lady didn't say anything! She just glared at me fiercely.

When The End appeared on the screen and the young lady stood up, I still didn't change my position. I looked at the lady again. She was about to walk out leisurely.

Film and Literary Taste 238

— Huang Zhenxia

(3) The Congress Dances (Dragon Soaring and Phoenix Dancing)

This is another Viennese film, a masterpiece of Wufat's Palace of Art, rich in sound, light, and color. Historical memories and fairy-tale fantasies unfold charmingly with the accompaniment of music. The performance is skilled, and the interpolation is vivid, especially the aftertaste. The historical background is 1814, just after the revolutionary tide of France was violently suppressed, and the autocratic demons of Europe once again appeared in broad daylight. At that time, that deformed child of the French Revolution—Napoleon Bonaparte—had been imprisoned on a remote island in the Mediterranean Sea. His religious-like army that swept across Europe was either buried under the icy rivers of Russia or stained the wilderness of Saxony red. In short, the cry for freedom and equality in France was no longer able to threaten the autocratic demons in the dark of night. Therefore, Vienna, known as the Holy Roman Empire, was singing and dancing, and all nations were coming to pay tribute, reaching its peak for a time. The unfolding of this story takes place around the Vienna Congress at its peak, and takes the glove shop girl, the "Cinderella" type played by Lili Hayworth, as the central figure, gently unfolding a fairy-tale romance. However, just as this little girl was hungrily dreaming of her "charming prince"—Tsar Alexander I—a storm suddenly rose in the Mediterranean Sea, and Napoleon had already raised his sweeping footsteps, re-trampling European soil with the frantic melody of the Marseillaise. Thus, the Vienna Congress quietly closed, and the elegant people dispersed like clouds, returning to their homelands to prepare for the battlefield of Waterloo. And the ending of this story is such a fairy-tale disillusionment. The glove shop girl (played by the genius Lili Hayworth), although she shed a few clear tears after waking up from her dream, soon returned to being a thorough Viennese little woman, lovable, playful, laughing wildly, and singing clearly...

The story is like this, the musical accompaniment has achieved great success, the light is bright in the spring, giving people a feeling of warmth under the sun everywhere. The director is extremely clever, and the actors are all talented. After watching it, one cannot help but develop a dislike for superficial American films.

This is "The Congress Dances," an extremely rare musical comedy.
